    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer639626768160249831">Three tales of supernatural love, each pivoting on a kiss that is no mere kiss, but an action with profound consequences for the kissers' souls:<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16079073.Goblin_Fruit' title='Goblin Fruit' rel='nofollow noopener'>Goblin Fruit</a><br/>In Victorian times, goblin men had only to offer young girls sumptuous fruits to tempt them to sell their souls.   <span id="freeText639626768160249831" style="display:none">Three tales of supernatural love, each pivoting on a kiss that is no mere kiss, but an action with profound consequences for the kissers' souls:<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16079073.Goblin_Fruit" title="Goblin Fruit" rel="nofollow noopener">Goblin Fruit</a><br />In Victorian times, goblin men had only to offer young girls sumptuous fruits to tempt them to sell their souls. But what does it take to tempt today's savvy girls?<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17704852.Spicy_Little_Curses" title="Spicy Little Curses" rel="nofollow noopener">Spicy Little Curses</a><br /> A demon and the ambassador to Hell tussle over the soul of a beautiful English girl in India. Matters become complicated when she falls in love and decides to test her curse.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17995785.Hatchling" title="Hatchling" rel="nofollow noopener">Hatchling</a><br />Six days before Esme's fourteenth birthday, her left eye turns from brown to blue. She little suspects what the change heralds, but her small safe life begins to unravel at once. What does the beautiful, fanged man want with her, and how is her fate connected to a mysterious race of demons?</span>
  <a data-text-id="639626768160249831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's about unusual human beings, tangled in the folk and myths Old Worlders grew up being told. There are short stories, beautifully written and fille<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's about unusual human beings, tangled in the folk and myths Old Worlders grew up being told. There are short stories, beautifully written and filled very unique characters (the friends and the foes as well). This stories are worth more time than the amount of it that it would take you to read them.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_154059619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154059619" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154059619?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who miss the days when authors wanted to be artists, not millionaires</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154059619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16452173476001237240"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Beautiful words, beautiful stories, beautiful characters... you know, this is just one damn beautiful book. I am in awe of it. Can you fall in love with a book? If so, I'm guilty. I don't mean to sound condescending to young adult readers (I am one) but this book simply does not deserve the readership that thought <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_' title='Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twilight</a> was the best book ever written. <br/><br/>Everything about the marketing and presentation of this book does not convey how truly wonderful it is. Firstly, though the cover illustrat</span>
  <span id="freeText16452173476001237240" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Beautiful words, beautiful stories, beautiful characters... you know, this is just one damn beautiful book. I am in awe of it. Can you fall in love with a book? If so, I'm guilty. I don't mean to sound condescending to young adult readers (I am one) but this book simply does not deserve the readership that thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> was the best book ever written. <br><br>Everything about the marketing and presentation of this book does not convey how truly wonderful it is. Firstly, though the cover illustration is a stunning work of art, I think it tends to immediately appeal to younger readers and rule out an older audience. It's pretty... but it looks like a children's book. Same with the title... it's cute, <i>very cute</i> and it's quite a subtle representation of what the book is about... but again, it sounds like a cutesy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>-style romance. Another thing it has in common with <i>the saga</i> is the genre it is categorised in: paranormal romance.<br><br>But to say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7638021.Lips_Touch_Three_Times" title="Lips Touch Three Times by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Lips Touch: Three Times</a> are both paranormal romances is like saying tin and platinum are both metals. <b>It's in an entirely different league</b>. And I almost didn't read this because I saw reviews saying the first story was just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>. <b>No, no, <i>no</i></b>. The very main difference between the two is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor" title="Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Laini Taylor</a> remembers the basic principle of quality writing.<br><br>Let's look at Bella Swan for a second... after four books what do we know about her?<br><br>1) She's that girl who's in love with a vampire<br>2) She's that girl who's in love with Edward Cullen<br>3) She's that girl... um, that's about it.<br><br>In one paragraph of that first story called 'Goblin Fruit', that according to some is "just like Twilight", this is Kizzy:<br><br><i>"Kizzy wanted to be a woman who would dive off the prow of a sailboat into the sea, who would fall back in a tangle of sheets, laughing, and who could dance a tango, lazily stroke a leopard with her bare foot, freeze an enemy's blood with her eyes, make promises she couldn't possibly keep, and then shift the world to keep them. She wanted to write memoirs and autograph them at a tiny bookshop in Rome, with a line of admirers snaking down a pink-lit alley. She wanted to make love on a balcony, ruin someone, trade in esoteric knowledge, watch strangers as coolly as a cat. She wanted to be inscrutable, have a drink named after her, a love song written for her, and a handsome adventurer's small airplane, champagne-christened <b>Kizzy</b>, which would vanish one day in a windstorm in Arabia so that she would have to mount a rescue operation involving camels, and wear an indigo veil against the stinging sand, just like the nomads. Kizzy <b>wanted</b>."</i><br><br>YES. In just one paragraph, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor" title="Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Laini Taylor</a> has created a far more complex character than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/941441.Stephenie_Meyer" title="Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephenie Meyer</a> ever managed. And let me just say, this book is hard to quote from because the entire thing is a quotable masterpiece, you can find something beautiful in <i>every single paragraph</i> on <i>every single page</i>. I actually took longer than it would normally take me to finish a 250 page young adult novel, and not because it was hard work, but because I would read a few sentences, think "wow", and go back and read it again. And again. My only fault with it is that I finished the last story and wanted to cry because there wasn't any more.<br><br>Who is this <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor" title="Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Laini Taylor</a> who seems to have appeared out of nowhere all of a sudden with her extraordinary writing and her pink hair? I don't know but I do know I'll be getting my hands on her future work if I have to sell my soul in exchange (yeah, that was a bit melodramatic but I haven't come out of fairyland yet). Read this, spread the word. 'tis fantastic!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16452173476001237240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_87033634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87033634" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87033634?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who love fairy tales and gorgeous writing</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      ALA's 10 Best for 2010
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=national-book-award">national-book-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87033634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5983936190104087116"><b>Update 4/23/2017. </b>"Hatchling" might be the best work of Taylor's to date.<br/><br/>I am familiar with YA literature enough to know how horribly, horribly wrong a collection of short stories about kissing can go (see, for example, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6382952.The_Eternal_Kiss_13_Vampire_Tales_of_Blood_and_Desire' title='The Eternal Kiss 13 Vampire Tales of Blood and Desire by Trisha Telep' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Eternal Kiss: 13 Vampire Tales of Blood and Desire</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7343947.Kisses_from_Hell' title='Kisses from Hell by Kristin Cast' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kisses from Hell</a>). Let me tell you, "Lips Touch" is not <i>that</i> kind of book. This book is simply magical.<br/><br/>Laini Taylor grabs your attention with the first lines:<br/><br/><i>There is a certain kind of girl the goblins crave. You could wa</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5983936190104087116" style="display:none"><b>Update 4/23/2017. </b>"Hatchling" might be the best work of Taylor's to date.<br /><br />I am familiar with YA literature enough to know how horribly, horribly wrong a collection of short stories about kissing can go (see, for example, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6382952.The_Eternal_Kiss_13_Vampire_Tales_of_Blood_and_Desire" title="The Eternal Kiss 13 Vampire Tales of Blood and Desire by Trisha Telep" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eternal Kiss: 13 Vampire Tales of Blood and Desire</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7343947.Kisses_from_Hell" title="Kisses from Hell by Kristin Cast" rel="nofollow noopener">Kisses from Hell</a>). Let me tell you, "Lips Touch" is not <i>that</i> kind of book. This book is simply magical.<br /><br />Laini Taylor grabs your attention with the first lines:<br /><br /><i>There is a certain kind of girl the goblins crave. You could walk across a high school campus and point them out: not her, not her, <b>her</b>. The pert, lovely ones with butterfly tattoos in secret places, sitting on their boyfriends' laps? No, not them. The girls <b>watching</b> the lovely ones sitting on their boyfriends' laps? Yes.</i><br /><br /><i>Them.</i><br /><br /><i>The goblins want girls who dream so hard about being pretty their yearning leaves a palpable trail, a scent goblin can follow like sharks on a soft bloom of blood. The girls with hungry eyes who pray each night to wake up as someone else. Urgent, unkissed, wishful girls.</i><br /><br /><i>Like Kizzy.</i><br /><br />How can you possibly resist this gorgeous writing? I know I couldn't. <br /><br />The book consists of 3 stories, or rather, fairy tales based on Irish, Hindu, and Zoroastrian folklore. Each tale is about a kiss, the kind of kiss that changes lives, turns the world upside down, a kiss that can kill or bring you back to life. <br /><br />The writing is superb, the descriptions are gorgeous and the mythologies Laini creates are unique and enchanting. There is passion and love and tenderness in these stories. I remember shivering and smiling at the end of each one. <br /><br />The book is also beautifully illustrated. The fairy tales are preceded by short graphic stories which do not reveal the content on the tales themselves, but serve as sort of pre-stories whose details are revealed in the main tales.<br /><br />My only complaint about "Lips Touch" is that there isn't more, otherwise the fairy tales are irresistible and delicious as the kisses they are about. This book is definitely one of the best I've read this year so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5983936190104087116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_143647339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143647339" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143647339?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=teen-faves">teen-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=hey-shorty">hey-shorty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143647339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8585788910694701079">i was not expecting to five-star this. i must confess - i hate the title and i hate the cover art (although i love the internal illustrations) <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699560._SX540_.jpg' width='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699561._SX540_.jpg' width='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>aren't those much better?? something about the color palette on the cover is upsetting, the covergirl looks vapid and whorish, and the title makes it seem like some teen heartthrob novel, which is it not. what it <i>is</i> is a sequence of three fairy tale-ish stories.<br/><br/>the first one is my favorite, and this one <i>is</i> a first-love story, so what? a frustrated girl fr</span>
  <span id="freeText8585788910694701079" style="display:none">i was not expecting to five-star this. i must confess - i hate the title and i hate the cover art (although i love the internal illustrations) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699560._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699561._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>aren't those much better?? something about the color palette on the cover is upsetting, the covergirl looks vapid and whorish, and the title makes it seem like some teen heartthrob novel, which is it not. what it <i>is</i> is a sequence of three fairy tale-ish stories.<br><br>the first one is my favorite, and this one <i>is</i> a first-love story, so what? a frustrated girl from an old-world gypsy family living in a regular all-american town who does not fit into the high school full of beautiful "normal" people until a handsome stranger appears. yeah, the skeleton of the story is your basic fairy tale archetype, but the language with which she structures it is perfectly modern and evolved into what comes across as a very contemporary story. <br><br>kizzy and her two friends have pitch-perfect exchanges and bantering sessions that just leap right off the page. her frustration and dissatisfaction and wanting are perfect and believable and i tore through the story, wanting to get to the end and not knowing what kind of resolution the author would choose. (the <i>perfect</i> one, of course!)<br><br>the supernatural elements of this story; the goblins and the fruit they try to force into the mouths of maidens - i mean, it's not a subtle metaphor, but the way this woman writes just carries the reader along in a wave of perfect phrasings.<br><br>here is an overlong passage you can either read or not.<br><br><i>kizzy had never met her - mairenni had stayed behind in the old country - but her grandmother said she looked like her. there was a single sepia photograph of a girl in a doorway, full-lipped, with eyes that seemed to sparkle with secrets. kizzy had always been fascinated by her - truth be told, she had always identified more with that wild girl who almost sold her soul for the taste of figs than with her grandmother who kept her lips tight shut and never hungered for forbidden things. but though she stared at that photo, and even saw the shape of her own eyes and lips mirrored back at her, kizzy just couldn't see herself in that long-ago girl, ripe and thrilling and flush with a weird species of beauty the young have no vocabulary for. <br><br>kizzy was so busy wishing she was sarah ferris or jenny glass that she could scarcely see herself at all, and she was certainly blind to her own weird beauty; her heavy, spell-casting eyes, too-wide mouth, wild hair, and hips that could be wild too, if they learned how. no one else in town looked anything like her, and if she lived to womanhood, she was the one artists would want to draw, not the sarahs and jennys. she was the one who would some day know a dozen ways to wear a silk scarf, how to read the sky for rain and coax feral animals near, how to purr throaty love songs in portuguese and basque, how to lay a vampire to rest, how to light a cigar, how to light a man's imagination on fire.<br>	<br>if she lived to womanhood.</i><br><br>the second story reads the most like a typical fairy tale, mixed with biblical and classical mythologies. the story of a woman cursed with silence, told that if she ever utters a sound, her voice will destroy all who hear it.she lives her life believing in this curse until her doubt is awakened by... a handsome stranger. the tension in this story is built up so carefully, raising questions about blind faith and trust vs. hard evidence, with some field trips to the underworld. this story, too, seems darker and sexier than most fairy tales, or at least more so than ones i would expect scholastic to publish. this is an applauding tone, not a critical one.<br><br>the third story is the longest, and reads more like a fantasy short story than a fairy tale. but that might just be my unfamiliarity with these particular themes. <br><br>most fairy tales are set in a recognizable location with some fantastical elements thrown in to make them more appealing to a younger audience, but not so fantastical that the moral or lesson is not recognized as being applicable to the real world.this one is all world-building and shapeshifting and body-snatching, with very little to anchor it in a recognizable environment. it is still great, it just didn't feel as much like a traditional fairy tale as the previous two.<br><br>this story is also a little bit creepy, and it is about possession and love and protection and selfishness and how both motherhood and romantic love relate to all of the above.<br><br>i am so grateful to ariel because when we were at the suzanne collins midnight magic party and i had to pick one hardcover book to buy to get my free mug, <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699562._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>she talked me into this one instead of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125858032" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>beautiful creatures</i>
</a> which has a beautiful cover, but is a way crappier book. she helped me dodge a bullet there because friends don't let friends buy crappy books on their birthday. plus, signed!! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699563.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>i am a happy girl.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_1993477579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993477579" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1993477579?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=mythology-folklore">mythology-folklore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1993477579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17809479684247349290"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cfBDwI-hQoY' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/KKRAz9D' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502728679i/23589160._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Nectar and spice, goblins and demons, memories and sorcery abound in three tales of supernatural love that hinge on a kiss that’s unlike any other kiss.<br/><br/>Readers who’ve only just begun to explore and fall head-over-heels for Laini Taylor’s recently released books will be equally enchanted by <i>Lips Touch Three Times</i>. Taylor employs an imaginative approach to writing that’s uniquely her own and, despite being</span>
  <span id="freeText17809479684247349290" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cfBDwI-hQoY" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/KKRAz9D" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502728679i/23589160._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nectar and spice, goblins and demons, memories and sorcery abound in three tales of supernatural love that hinge on a kiss that’s unlike any other kiss.<br><br>Readers who’ve only just begun to explore and fall head-over-heels for Laini Taylor’s recently released books will be equally enchanted by <i>Lips Touch Three Times</i>. Taylor employs an imaginative approach to writing that’s uniquely her own and, despite being one of her earliest published works (first released in 2009), <i>Lips Touch Three Times</i> is no exception. <br><br>Drawing inspiration from mythology, fantasy, and various religions, Taylor crafts a spellbinding array of characters and locales. She enriches her creations by embroidering everything from the tangible, such as characters or clothing, to the intangible, like dreams or desire, with words evocative of mysticism, whimsy, and romanticism. <br><br><i>His eyes, very dark, canted elvishly upward at the outer corners and were surrounded by delicate bruises of sleeplessness, bluish and tender, giving him the look – [she] fancied – of a poet who had been up all night with a candle and a quill, memorializing a beautiful lady who had fallen from the aristocracy to die penniless of a fever, perhaps in a snowbank, leaving, of course, an ethereal corpse.</i> <br><br>While Taylor’s stylistic writing flair remains wonderfully consistent throughout, each of the protagonists in her stories infuse the narrative with their own individuality and longing. <br><br>In "Goblin Fruit," Kizzy is a seemingly average teenage girl, relegated to hovering in the shadowy corners of her high school where she watches the attractive popular students from afar. She’s unaware that her “<i>spell-casting eyes</i>” and “<i>wild hair, and hips that could be wild too, if they learned how</i>” make her a natural beauty. Where her dislikes are parochial – her unruly hair, her ankles, being seen in public with family members – Kizzy’s desires are far more sophisticated: <br><br><i>She wanted to make love on a balcony, ruin someone, trade in esoteric knowledge, watch strangers as coolly as a cat. She wanted to be inscrutable, have a drink named after her, a love song written for her, and a handsome adventurer’s small airplane, champagne-christened</i> Kizzy<i>, which would vanish one day in a windstorm in Arabia so that she would have to mount a rescue operation involving camels, and wear an indigo veil against the stinging sand, just like the nomads.</i> <br><br>Kizzy’s family is just as unorthodox and strange. They prefer singing songs in a foreign, unknown language over watching television, and Kizzy’s grandmother tells stories of goblins luring young maidens with luscious fruit then slowly sipping at their souls until the maidens wither their way to an early death. What her grandmother doesn’t tell her is that goblins have the power to shape-shift, so when a new boy of unparalleled attractiveness arrives at Kizzy’s school and takes a special interest in her, she’s not inclined to question whether he could be the death of her . . . <br><br>"Spicy Little Curses Such As These" introduces Anamique (Ana), a young beauty with eyes that are “<i>lonely, and haunted, and hungry</i>” because she has reason to believe she was cursed by a demon to never speak. Fearful that uttering so much as one word will kill everyone within earshot, she goes a lifetime refraining from using her voice. <br><br><i>She kept her own voice like a bird in a cage. She imagined it as a willful songbird with a puffed breast, its feathers gray like her eyes, with a flash of peacock blue at the neck, and the cage an ornate prison of rusted scrollwork with a little latched door that she never dared open. Sometimes the urge to do so was nearly overpowering.</i> <br><br>When a handsome young soldier enters her life, Ana yearns to speak aloud her love for him and begins to question the validity of the curse. If she’s wrong about the curse, then her voice can at last be set free; but if she’s right, then an utterance of love will kill the man who is her heart’s greatest desire . . . <br><br>Finally, "Hatchling" puts forth a red-haired girl with porcelain skin named Esmé whose entire world is upended by one small, unexpected change: <br><br><i>Six days before Esmé’s fourteenth birthday, her left eye turned from brown to blue. It happened in the night. She went to sleep with brown eyes, and when she woke at dawn to the howling of wolves, her left eye was</i> blue<i>.</i> <br><br>The reason for Esmé’s transient London-life with her mother is unveiled in this multi-layered story that not only crosses the known world with mythical realms, it explores the idea of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ shared memories <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Readers will pass through one diaphanous veil after another while traveling alongside Esmé as she wades through her memories and navigates the unbridled intensity found in a kiss . . . <br><br>With first kisses being central to all three stories, <i>Lips Touch Three Times</i> has plentiful imagery that speaks of virginity, fertility, and sexual appetite. By bestowing the narrative with mention of plump fruits, hungry mouths, and tongues getting a first taste, Taylor successfully portrays passion and sexual desire without resorting to more gratuitous measures. <br><br>Further enhancing the book’s succulence are the vividly rendered illustrations created by Taylor’s husband, artist Jim Di Bartolo. His hyper-stylized representation of caged birds, flame-licked demons, and defiant maidens – set against a backdrop of gray and blushing with pinks and reds – accurately capture the sorrowful nature of Taylor’s stories. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357928i/709131._SX540_.jpg" width="397" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What is arguably the book’s only weakness is more than made up for by Di Bartolo’s artistry: <i>Goblin Fruit</i> feels incomplete, but an arresting illustration at the end of the story provides a sense of closure. <br><br>Filled with mystery and magic, and glowing with the gloomy, fanciful elegance that’s the hallmark of Laini Taylor’s linguistic genius, <i>Lips Touch Three Times</i> is a dazzling collection of short stories.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17809479684247349290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_154304556" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154304556" />
    <a title="Lamia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4804393-lamia"><img alt="Lamia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294943987p2/4804393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154304556?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lamia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lamia" href="/user/show/4804393-lamia">Lamia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=own-hardcopy">own-hardcopy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154304556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6173838291266390897">This can also be seen at <a href='http://the-book-eater.blogspot.com/2011/03/review-lips-touch-three-times-by-laini.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <u>The Book Eater</u>
</a><br/><br/>I truly feel like anything I say couldn't do this book justice.<br/>So, in my endeavor to describe my *cough* "feelings", I made a pie chart (I love pie charts).<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346958i/701319.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book was was <i>amazing</i>. Well-written. Gorgeous, gorgeous writing. Touching characters. I just... I loved it. Every story was better than the last. Enchanting, horrifying, beautiful and captivating. The way Taylor writes... Again, I don't know what to say. She pulls you into the universe she create</span>
  <span id="freeText6173838291266390897" style="display:none">This can also be seen at <a href="http://the-book-eater.blogspot.com/2011/03/review-lips-touch-three-times-by-laini.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>The Book Eater</u>
</a><br><br>I truly feel like anything I say couldn't do this book justice.<br>So, in my endeavor to describe my *cough* "feelings", I made a pie chart (I love pie charts).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346958i/701319.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was was <i>amazing</i>. Well-written. Gorgeous, gorgeous writing. Touching characters. I just... I loved it. Every story was better than the last. Enchanting, horrifying, beautiful and captivating. The way Taylor writes... Again, I don't know what to say. She pulls you into the universe she created like no others and makes you truly experience the story she's telling. Her writing grabs you and doesn't let you go. You get attached to the characters, feel their joy and their horror, all the while sinking deeper and deeper into the mesmerizing universe she presents you with.<br><br>The way she manages to combine such a vast array of emotion into one story is mind boggling. This book feels like a rainy afternoon spent cuddled up in your blankets with an amazing book and a tub of ice cream. It's a treat you've been waiting for, and savor slowly to keep it as long as possible. It's the kind of book you keep reading at night, secretly, while you're supposed to be sleeping simply because you just can't stop reading. <br><br>While the first story was short, sensual and surprising, the second and third ones were longer, and therefore had their own universe and set of rules. And the writing. God. Her prose is lyrical and flows perfectly. She uses recurrent imagery so well that you can almost picture everything. I kept literally stopping in the middle of a chapter to think "wow, this sentence is gorgeous."<br><br>Also, I'd just like to point out that not once, while reading this book did I think anything was remotely wrong with the character development, the pacing, the plot or just... anything. This is rare, people. Very rare. Everything made perfect sense. So much sense, actually, that when Taylor later explains her definition of the "Hell" she used in the second story, it wasn't necessary, because she told it in such a way that it was obvious for anyone, even those not versed in Hindu beliefs like me.<br><br>If you're still not convinced, here's a quote:<br><br><i>"[...] they thought the same thoughts as completely as if a butterfly traveled back and forth between their minds, bearing ideas on its legs like pollen."</i><br><br>See? So pretty. So cute and perfect. Sigh.<br><br>Really. I'm re-reading myself and I have <i>not</i> done this story justice. Don't take my words for it. Go read it. You won't be sorry.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_99371141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99371141" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99371141?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone with the capacity for beauty and romance, pain and loss.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99371141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3062967521766299436">To those of you who haven't read this book, what are you doing right now? If your answer is anything other than "Purchasing this book and getting ready to read it" then I'm afraid that you and I might just have to come to some kind of disagreement.<br/><br/>There is something enchantingly, alluringly fantastic about this book. From it's beautifully written stories to the amazing drawings and the characters within. This book is like a beautiful, wild romani woman with her ankle bracelets, bare feet and twi</span>
  <span id="freeText3062967521766299436" style="display:none">To those of you who haven't read this book, what are you doing right now? If your answer is anything other than "Purchasing this book and getting ready to read it" then I'm afraid that you and I might just have to come to some kind of disagreement.<br><br>There is something enchantingly, alluringly fantastic about this book. From it's beautifully written stories to the amazing drawings and the characters within. This book is like a beautiful, wild romani woman with her ankle bracelets, bare feet and twirling skirts. Mysterious, beautiful, dangerous and entrancing. <br><br>Not that Babcia approves of gypsies. Apparently they stole her chickens during the war and she's never forgiven them since. True story. She never rants about the Germans, she'll tell you that the Russians are worse but if you even mention the Gypsies she'll start a Polish rant the likes of which my Irish born and bred self had never imagined until I saw it with my own eyes. Though apparently gypsy tears are THE thing this season to put in your charms.<br><br>Why can't other female protagonists in YA literature be as awesome as the girls in this? I had a fangirl try to tell me that Luce from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_" title="Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen</a> was a real girl, and therefor relatable, because she was a spineless, boring teenage moron. Well, I think Laini Taylor just provided the ultimate bitch slap to that theory. Kizzy was a hundred times more relatable and real without the downside of being so miserably pathetic that she'll probably be doing Daniel Gregori's gardening in a slutty maid outfit just so he'll acknowledge her existence.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Oops... too late.<br><br>Well, at least she isn't some deranged and mentally unstable stalker without a shred of dignity like Nora from <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_" title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush, Hush</a>!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>*Cough* Moving on...<br><br>You know what I love the best about this book - the inevitable Europeanness of it all. Even when she didn't mean to. I mean, the stories mostly ended out happy or open ended but there were consequences or time lost or bargains made or things given over. Nobody turned into a vampire without any consequences, gave birth a lochness monster and then defeated the bad guys without a single blow.<br><br>It was all so gritty and filled with sacrifices, loss, but redemption and possibility.<br><br><span>[image error]</span> <br><br>But not in that way...<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3062967521766299436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always"><img alt="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562987681p2/5478965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1367202808?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always">Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=insta-love-lust-attraction">insta-love-lust-attraction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=might-make-you-shit-bricks">might-make-you-shit-bricks</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367202808" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8665749389736822905"><b>Overall:</b><br/><br/><strong>Laini Taylor is a master of crafting darkly gorgeous and deliciously unique tales</strong> with all sorts of unearthly creatures. Each story featured strong heroines with very different personalities, and the same goes for the men they touch lips with.<br/><br/>As usual, it was hard to get into her very flowery and descriptive writing, but nevertheless I enjoyed <em>Lips Touch: Three Times</em> as a whole.<br/><br/><b>Goblin Fruit: (4 stars)</b><br/><br/>Laini Taylor works magic with this story. I mean, who else can create such beautiful, ee</span>
  <span id="freeText8665749389736822905" style="display:none"><b>Overall:</b><br /><br /><strong>Laini Taylor is a master of crafting darkly gorgeous and deliciously unique tales</strong> with all sorts of unearthly creatures. Each story featured strong heroines with very different personalities, and the same goes for the men they touch lips with.<br /><br />As usual, it was hard to get into her very flowery and descriptive writing, but nevertheless I enjoyed <em>Lips Touch: Three Times</em> as a whole.<br /><br /><b>Goblin Fruit: (4 stars)</b><br /><br />Laini Taylor works magic with this story. I mean, who else can create such beautiful, eerie tale with depth in just 54 pages?<br /><br />The actual story was so<strong> dark and whimsical</strong>; you can't not get sucked into it. We're told of goblins, ghosts, swan wings in coffins with the dead--all of those disturbing bedtime stories rolled into one.<br /><br />Our main character,<strong> Kizzy, was so well-developed and realistic.</strong> She's a girl with dreams and so many <i>wants</i>, just like all of us. She also has a "love interest" here, and I did ship them pretty early on.<br /><br />Again, the only reason I didn't love this was because of the writing. <strong>The flowery writing worked well with the story,</strong> but not with my brain, and the humor was lost on me.<br /><br /><b>Spicy Little Curses Such As These: (2 stars)</b><br /><br />Short Story Syndrome (I'm totally making this up) has finally caught up, and <strong>the insta-love in this story hits me hard</strong>.<br /><br />The writing was somewhat harder to get into in this one as well, probably because a lot of it also takes part in the real world (AKA not Hell) so the flowery writing didn't work for me in those parts.<br /><br />I couldn't get a sense of the characters too much, either.<strong> Anamique lacked a strong personality</strong> for me, and I can't say anything much about her aside from the fact that she's gorgeous and has a lovely singing voice. I found James to be dull as well.<br /><br />Despite those, as usual, Laini Taylor weaved together an absolutely stunning story. It started off and ended equally fabulously--no spoilers though!<br /><br /><b>Hatchling: (3.5 stars)</b><br /><br />"Hatchling" is the longest of the short stories featured in <em>Lips Touch: Three Times</em>, and it's certainly the one with most depth as well. <strong>It was weird, odd and disturbing,</strong> but in a totally holy-cow-how-are-you-such-a-genius-Laini kind of way.<br /><br />It features Esme, a young heroine with a dark past--and a dark <em>present</em>. You're going to discover the truth behind her "condition" along with her, not before or after.<br /><br />There were three romances in this story, two that I didn't care for, and one that didn't really play a big role in the story but I adored dearly.<strong> The romances were realistic,</strong> though, although I don't think I can mention in what way in fear of spoilers.<br /><br />Laini Taylor weaves such <strong>unique mythology and intricate details</strong> in this short story, sometimes a bit too detailed for a reader with goldfish attention span like me, but enchanting for the most part.<br /><br /><a href="http://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadly Darlings</a> | <a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Social Potato</a> | <a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Geek</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/aimeereads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/aimeereads" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_1673065859" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1673065859" />
    <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda"><img alt="Arah-Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601299926p2/5859453.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arah-Lynda" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda">Arah-Lynda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1673065859" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4880020888151251150">Boy howdy! Where did this goddess of words with the pink hair come from? I am not usually a big fan of the short story, but I do declare, I will read anything this literary seductress writes, even her stroked out grocery list, so send them on down, and I will eat them up. <br/><br/>Why oh why, would I, with my meagre abilities, even try, to persuade you to read these stories, each of which involve a kiss, when Laini herself awards us a brief glimpse of what is to come.<br/><br/><br/><b>Goblin Fruit</b> (my favourite)<br/><br/><i>There is a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4880020888151251150" style="display:none">Boy howdy! Where did this goddess of words with the pink hair come from? I am not usually a big fan of the short story, but I do declare, I will read anything this literary seductress writes, even her stroked out grocery list, so send them on down, and I will eat them up. <br /><br />Why oh why, would I, with my meagre abilities, even try, to persuade you to read these stories, each of which involve a kiss, when Laini herself awards us a brief glimpse of what is to come.<br /><br /><br /><b>Goblin Fruit</b> (my favourite)<br /><br /><i>There is a certain kind of girl the goblins crave. You could walk across a high school campus and point them out: not her, not her, <b>her</b>. The pert, lovely ones with butterfly tattoos in secret places, sitting on their boyfriends’ laps? No, not them. The girls <u>watching</u> the lovely ones sitting on their boyfriends’ laps? Yes.<br />Them.<br /><br />The goblins want girls who dream so hard about being pretty their yearning leaves a palpable trail, a scent goblins can follow like sharks on a soft bloom of blood. The girls with hungry eyes who pray each night to wake up as someone else. Urgent, unkissed, wishful girls.<br />Like Kizzy. <br /><br />Kizzy wanted it all so bad her soul leaned half out of her body hungering after it, and that was what drove the goblins wild, her soul hanging out there like an untucked shirt.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>Spicy Little Curses</b><br /><br /><i>Kissing can ruin lives. Lips touch, sometimes teeth clash. New hunger is born with a throb and caution falls away. A cursed girl with lips moist from her first kiss might feel suddenly wild, like a little monsoon. She might forget her curse just long enough to get careless and let it come true. She might kill every-one she loves.<br /><br />She might and she might not.<br /><br />A particular demon in India rather hoped she would. <br /><br />This is the story of the curse and the kiss, the demon and the girl. It’s a love story with dancing and death in it, and singing and souls and shadows reeled out on kite strings. It begins underneath India, on the cusp of the last century when the British were still riding elephants with maharajas and skirmishing on the arid frontiers of the empire.<br /><br />The story begins in Hell.</i><br /><br /> <br /><b>Hatchling</b><br /><br /><i>Six days before Esme’s fourteenth birthday, her left eye turned from brown to blue. It happened in the night. She went to sleep with brown eyes, and when she woke at dawn to the howling of wolves, her left eye was blue. She had just slipped out of bed when she noticed it. She was headed to the window to look for the wolves – wolves in London, of all impossible things! But she didn’t make it to the window. Her eye flashed at her in the mirror, pale as the wink of a ghost, and she forgot all about the wolves and stared at herself.<br /><br />It was no trick of the light. Her eye was an eerie white-blue, the color of ancient ice in a place that never thaws, and as startling as it was, there was something profoundly familiar about it too. Esme’s blood quickened as a shock of memories pulsed through her: a world of snow and spires; a milky mirror framed in jewels; the touch of warm lips on hers.<br /><br />Esme swayed on her feet. These weren’t her memories. This wasn’t her eye. She clamped a hand over it and ran to wake her mother.</i> <br /><br /><br /><br />As a prelude to each of these stories Jim Di Bartolo graces these pages with graphic illustrations, which in themselves are well worth the price of admission. <br /><br />Gather round boys and girls and listen to these fairy tale type stories from a writer of unparalleled imagination and singular panache. <br /><br /> Woot! Woot! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4880020888151251150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_170590641" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170590641" />
    <a title="Meredith Holley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley"><img alt="Meredith Holley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548641865p2/1302775.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170590641?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith Holley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith Holley" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley">Meredith Holley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Linda</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Meredith by: </span>
      Thomas Tomato
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=chosen-girls">chosen-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=girls-rule">girls-rule</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=classic-young-adult">classic-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=pacific-northwest-glory">pacific-northwest-glory</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170590641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1981583708666295230">When you want to take a story that someone else has told and make it your own, do it like this. If you want to write a story, recognize your own magic, your own style, and add it to the story you want to steal. If you want to write a story, do what Laini Taylor did, and absorb the story, wait until it has seeped into the interstitial places of your writing, and give it back to your reader. Make it beautiful and true. And the only way you can do that is by figuring out what to you is beauty and t</span>
  <span id="freeText1981583708666295230" style="display:none">When you want to take a story that someone else has told and make it your own, do it like this. If you want to write a story, recognize your own magic, your own style, and add it to the story you want to steal. If you want to write a story, do what Laini Taylor did, and absorb the story, wait until it has seeped into the interstitial places of your writing, and give it back to your reader. Make it beautiful and true. And the only way you can do that is by figuring out what to you is beauty and truth. So many writers try to figure out what made something beautiful to someone else. They try to say, what made <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12914.The_Aeneid" rel="nofollow noopener">the Trojan war beautiful to Homer</a>? What made <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/256683.City_of_Bones" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter beautiful to J.K. Rowling</a>? And they try to imitate that. They don’t say, "What makes this story beautiful to me?" Well, Laini Taylor told us what makes these stories beautiful to her.<br /><br />So, I’m a little expansive tonight. I’m a little drunk. I’m not usually one of those drunks who goes around telling everyone she loves them. In fact, I’ve been told I can recite a pretty good story while drunk, even if I don’t remember it a few months later. I usually don’t remember who I told stories to anyway, drunk or not drunk, no offense. Anyway, I just want to give this book a hug and tell it I love it. I love you, book. Like, in the full, Wayne’s World sense of the word. I love you, book. Damn, every time I write “book,” I spell it “bood.” Sorry. <br /><br />I love this book in a drunk, college-high-school kind of way. I love this book like, “Wait a second, what have we all be doing, standing around fighting over whether vampires are sparkly or not?” So, it turns out there are people out there writing real love stories and fairy tales. There are people reading great writing like Christina Rossetti’s <i>Goblin Market</i>, getting inspired by them, and then writing these wonderful tributes to them. <br /><br />I think, when anyone writes anything great, their ultimate hope has to be in some kind of legacy. They have to hope that their great writing will inspire something beautiful in the future, some kind of strength and inspiration. I think it is a tribute to the traditions that Rossetti, Hinduism, and Zoroastrianism created that Taylor could create something as beautiful as this book. And then, hopefully her writings will inspire someone else, and the stories of goblins, hell, and eternal life will continue. It is like how Shakespeare reminded us that 13-year-olds falling in love doesn’t always end for the best. And, look, that story has <a>continued in tradition</a> because of him. Hopefully we will all, likewise, remember not to eat goblin fruit because of Taylor, not to doubt our own curses or our own mortality.<br /><br />I had intended to talk about how some authors are natural with language, and how some authors know how to integrate a magical, traditional feeling with really modern writing. I don’t really feel like talking about that now that I am writing this. Maybe I will have more to say about that in the morning. Anyway, it’s not like Taylor tried to add a bunch of ‘ye’s to her writing, or like she tried to end everything with “e” like, unfortunately, some authors do, to give a sense of ye olde timmes. Taylor shows everything beautifully, and in doing so she shows how “modern times” are not removed from tradition and magick(e).<br /><br />I like how this book is not about kisses, is not about love. When I first picked it up I thought it would be an emo version of Gossip Girl, but it is not that. It is about evil kisses, lips shutting in silence, and kisses that are sense memory. I like how this book is about loyalty and strength. I like how it is about curses. This book is beautiful, and in true, drunken or non-drunken spirit, I love it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1981583708666295230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1960633320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1960633320" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1960633320?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-buylist">x-buylist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-notowned">y-notowned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=what-is-this-mess">what-is-this-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=author-love">author-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1960633320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14234062839768580981">This is a story collection that I have very mixed feelings on, so <b>I'll be color-coding my thoughts</b>. ♔ will be for praise, ♚ will be for criticism. <br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>GENERAL REVIEW</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>♔ <b>The writing is luscious and beautiful</b>, with great atmosphere and tone. Maybe not <i>quite</i> as spectacular as her later writing, but she's definitely showing a great beginning here. And I love the addition of artwork!! I mean, just look at this. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699560._SX540_.jpg' width='500' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>♚ In general, <b>this is a really great piece of 2000s YA</b>. Unfortunately... <b>it is also </b></span>
  <span id="freeText14234062839768580981" style="display:none">This is a story collection that I have very mixed feelings on, so <b>I'll be color-coding my thoughts</b>. ♔ will be for praise, ♚ will be for criticism. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>GENERAL REVIEW</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>♔ <b>The writing is luscious and beautiful</b>, with great atmosphere and tone. Maybe not <i>quite</i> as spectacular as her later writing, but she's definitely showing a great beginning here. And I love the addition of artwork!! I mean, just look at this. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344685i/699560._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>♚ In general, <b>this is a really great piece of 2000s YA</b>. Unfortunately... <b>it is also a piece of 2000s YA</b>. I'm sure this could be considered awesome feminist lit back in 2009, but between some of the fatshaming, <b>I'm-not-like-other-girls</b> mentality, and weird <b>exoticism / appropriation of Indian mythology</b> - we'll discuss this a bit later - I found myself getting just a <i>bit</i> annoyed. Or maybe a little more than a bit. <br><br>♔ <b>Taylor's characterization is good</b>. She's great at conveying entire swaths of characterization in just one or two lines, which is an excellent trait for a short story collection and one I think I noticed more.<br><br>♚ <b>It's just not <i>quite</i> as good.</b> The characterization shown here would've stood out in the 2009 YA world; I don't think it does anymore, whether because of short form or because of overall quality. I think she's quite improved on characterization and writing as she's grown; this book just doesn't deliver to the same degree as her later <i>Strange the Dreamer</i>. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>STORY REVIEWS</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br># <i>Goblin Fruit</i>: This is a story you have to read to the end, because 98% of my enjoyment of this came from the final page. Unfortunately, I was not a fan of the dialogue - it felt quite cheesy compared to some of the Zuzana / Karou dialogue in Taylor's later <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> trilogy. I also wasn't a fan of some of the borderline fatshaming and definite vibe of I'm-not-like-other-girls. <br><br># <i>Spicy Little Curses Such as These</i>: I have... very mixed feelings on this. I liked the writing more than I did for <i>Goblin Fruit</i>, as it fell closer to Taylor's later prose, and I thought the character work was great. The ending was especially fabulous.<br><br>And yet... <b>holy shit, the cultural stuff is bad.</b> I'm sorry, but setting your story in India for the mythology - not only that, fucking <i>colonial</i> India - and having your entire cast be white European colonists? Not a good look. Not a good look at all. It made me <i>super</i> uncomfortable to even read this. You can tell from the <i>title</i> that this is going to be a oh-India-is-so-exotic circlejerk, and it completely lives up to that.<br><br># <i>Hatchling</i>: This was probably my favorite; it's the one where the writing and character work is strongest and closest to her later works. The only thing is, um... <b>this basically feels like softcore DoSaB.</b> The plot and character concepts are in some ways <i>so</i> similar to her later books that I don't think this felt new to me. <br><br>VERDICT: Some good thoughts, and I definitely understand the hype, but too many issues for me to really love this. It was definitely interesting to see how Laini Taylor has evolved as an author; you can see that it's the same author, yet her later books just have another level of depth that isn't so present here. <br><br><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14234062839768580981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead">Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer177360061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2201238855387397787">Hubby... just put the NFL network on, he'll forget I'm alive.<br/>Kids.... they can fend for themselves.<br/>laundry, soaking wet in the washing machine... I'll wash it twice, no one will ever know.<br/>Dishes.... that is what paper plates are for.<br/><br/>I initially read around 35 pages and knew I had something special. I planned on finishing story #1 and that was it. Like a magic spell, I picked up the book and not only finished the other stories but did not move my ass at all from my little corner on the coach. My </span>
  <span id="freeText2201238855387397787" style="display:none">Hubby... just put the NFL network on, he'll forget I'm alive.<br />Kids.... they can fend for themselves.<br />laundry, soaking wet in the washing machine... I'll wash it twice, no one will ever know.<br />Dishes.... that is what paper plates are for.<br /><br />I initially read around 35 pages and knew I had something special. I planned on finishing story #1 and that was it. Like a magic spell, I picked up the book and not only finished the other stories but did not move my ass at all from my little corner on the coach. My dog did try to get me to move as evident of her collection of toys all over my legs and couch but I wasn't buying her game. This was major selfish "me" time!<br /><br />Ok, back to the book. 1st time authors, if you want like a "how to" guide, check out Laini Taylor. Her words are so beautiful. You know how when you do a review you want to share maybe a line or two from the book, to show off how well the author writes? Well, I kept thinking, this would be a great line, nope, this one is even better. No, this IS the one. I then realized the entire book is made up of lines that deserve to be read, highlighted and shared by everyone.<br /><br />I will not only keep this book but it will be shared with my kids and hopefully with their kids. I never thought I'd say that about a book that wasn't already labeled a "classic". So, what am I trying to say....<br /><br />Go read this book. I'll stand by my recommendation until the last page!<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203523874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17769469701408261712">Three stories. Three girls. One thing in common: each lady has not been kissed. And their first taste of that special time when lips touch won't come without a price . . .<br/><br/>The wife and husband team of Laini Taylor and Jim Di Bartolo sure do make for a sumptuous collection of stories. I'd be hard-pressed to choose which is more beautiful: Taylor's writing or Di Bartolo's illustrations.<br/><br/>Let me give you samples of each:<br/><br/><i>"With a deep, visceral ache, she wished her true form might prove to be a sleek an</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17769469701408261712" style="display:none">Three stories. Three girls. One thing in common: each lady has not been kissed. And their first taste of that special time when lips touch won't come without a price . . .<br><br>The wife and husband team of Laini Taylor and Jim Di Bartolo sure do make for a sumptuous collection of stories. I'd be hard-pressed to choose which is more beautiful: Taylor's writing or Di Bartolo's illustrations.<br><br>Let me give you samples of each:<br><br><i>"With a deep, visceral ache, she wished her true form might prove to be a sleek and shining one, like a stiletto blade slicing free of an ungainly sheath. Like a bird of prey losing its hatchling fluff to hunt in cold, magnificent skies. That she might become something glitering, something startling, something dangerous."</i><br><br><i>"Kissing can ruin lives. Lips touch, sometimes teeth clash. New hunger is born with a throb and caution falls away."</i><br><br><i>"And Esmé remembered in a rush - the wolfsong, the haunting, lyrical spirals of it in the dawn quiet and the feeling of euphoria that had attended it. Even in recollection the howling uplifted her like the crescendo at the end of a symphony and made her heartbeat quicken."</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357928i/709131._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(<i>I</i> would eat their fruit . . .)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357928i/709132._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(These are even more gorgeous in person . . .)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357928i/709133._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Makes you want to have red hair . . .)<br><br>Now, if those stunning snippets aren't enough to make you want to read this, <s>there's something wrong with you</s> I don't see how anything I can say will convince you to read this.<br><br><i>Very</i> close to four stars . . . 3.5. Definitely recommended.</span>
