<div id="review_155325356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155325356" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155325356?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everybody!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Vinaya by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=hmm-that-was-interesting">hmm-that-was-interesting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=i-ll-stalk-you-til-you-read-it">i-ll-stalk-you-til-you-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=speshul-snowflake">speshul-snowflake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-loved">books-i-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=the-real-5-star-deal">the-real-5-star-deal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155325356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17543190295457918341">I read the first story in Lips Touch about two months ago. It was... interesting. The writing was great, very picturesque, but the story per se didn't meet the expectations I had set for it after reading all the rave reviews on Goodreads. So I put the book aside for a while and finally picked it up yesterday when I was sitting in my new workplace with nothing else to do. I was Blown. Away.<br/><br/>Reading Lips Touch is like peeling an orange. At first, you break the skin, and you can feel the soft pulp u</span>
  <span id="freeText17543190295457918341" style="display:none">I read the first story in Lips Touch about two months ago. It was... interesting. The writing was great, very picturesque, but the story per se didn't meet the expectations I had set for it after reading all the rave reviews on Goodreads. So I put the book aside for a while and finally picked it up yesterday when I was sitting in my new workplace with nothing else to do. I was Blown. Away.<br /><br />Reading Lips Touch is like peeling an orange. At first, you break the skin, and you can feel the soft pulp underneath, smell the sharp tang of the juice and savour the anticipation of what is to come. This, for me, was the function that <i>Goblin Fruit</i> served. There was beautiful prose, haunting imagery and amazing characterization, but the oomph factor was yet to come...<br /><br />And then, two months later, I got to <i>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</i>. Now, as an Indian, I am understandably critical of books that are set in India, and use Indian mythology. Too many books about the colonial period tend to be either corrective or apologist, and I hate that authors want to change history like that. Laini Taylor, however, got it just right. Her writing was not flowery and overly descriptive, but in a rarely-seen display of skill, she managed to convey the hot, arid, uneasy atmosphere of colonial India with a few well-placed words. I could almost <i>see</i> the British with their desperately superior attitude, their discomfort with the foreignness of the land they were living in, their disdain for an Englishwoman who had 'gone native'. This might actually be my favourite story of the three simply because it portrays the setting and atmosphere of the entire story so very beautifully. <br /><br />Hatchling was a revelation of its own sort. The sheer diversity of Taylor's work makes me want to love her forever and ever. From Middle European mythology, to Hindu and Zoroastrian, she manages to subtly pick and choose her cultures without drowning the reader in a sea of unfamiliar information. What also truly astounded me about this story is that Taylor manages to weave three separate stories into one short story. That takes skill... and balls. You go, girl!<br /><br />The deceptively simple narrative hides a host of very subtle, very beautiful undertones that capture the imagination and the intellect. Lips Touch is truly a work of art, not to be missed by those of you laggards as are still on the fence about reading this book. Go. Now. Read it!<br /><br />P.S. Thank you Tatiana for recommending this amazing book to me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17543190295457918341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1014271233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1014271233" />
    <a title="Toni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24617462-toni"><img alt="Toni" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1014271233?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toni" href="/user/show/24617462-toni">Toni</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6513407631750777703">Look at this quote:<br/><br/><i>“Kizzy wanted to be a woman who would dive off the prow of a sailboat into the sea, who would fall back in a tangle of sheets, laughing, and who could dance a tango, lazily stroke a leopard with her bare foot, freeze an enemy's blood with her eyes, make promises she couldn't possibly keep, and then shift the world to keep them. She wanted to write memoirs and autograph them at a tiny bookshop in Rome, with a line of admirers snaking down a pink-lit alley. She wanted to make lo</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6513407631750777703" style="display:none">Look at this quote:<br><br><i>“Kizzy wanted to be a woman who would dive off the prow of a sailboat into the sea, who would fall back in a tangle of sheets, laughing, and who could dance a tango, lazily stroke a leopard with her bare foot, freeze an enemy's blood with her eyes, make promises she couldn't possibly keep, and then shift the world to keep them. She wanted to write memoirs and autograph them at a tiny bookshop in Rome, with a line of admirers snaking down a pink-lit alley. She wanted to make love on a balcony, ruin someone, trade in esoteric knowledge, watch strangers as coolly as a cat. She wanted to be inscrutable, have a drink named after her, a love song written for her, and a handsome adventurer's small airplane, champagne-christened Kizzy, which would vanish one day in a windstorm in Arabia so that she would have to mount a rescue operation involving camels, and wear an indigo veil against the stinging sand, just like the nomads.<br><u>Kizzy wanted.<u>”</u></u></i><br><br>The amount of characterization found in that one quote, on that one page, can put most of the books on my shelves to shame. Laini Taylor crafts worlds, storylines and characters with so much talent, they play out in your head like vivid dreams in which you feel everything, you can touch everything she describes and be everything she creates. <br><b>She's so good it hurts.</b><br><br>This collection of short stories again proves that she can turn the slightest legends into powerful stories and can make a very minimum amount of pages feel like a complex adventure. The writing is brilliant and the art (by her husband) is a beautiful addition.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357928i/709131._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The first story- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16079073.Goblin_Fruit" title="Goblin Fruit by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Goblin Fruit</a> was the shortest but my favorite. It had all the elements that I love in a story and an inconclusive ending that felt appropriate and somehow charming. <b>5 Stars it is.</b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17704852.Spicy_Little_Curses" title="Spicy Little Curses by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Spicy Little Curses</a> took me a few chapters to really get into but I loved it by the end. <b>4,5 Stars</b> and a whole lot of love.<br><br><i>“This is the story of the curse and the kiss, the demon and the girl. It's a love story with dancing and death in it, and singing and souls and shadows reeled out on kite strings.”</i><br><br>The last and the longest <u>Hatchling</u> was my least favorite but that doesn't mean that much. It was slower at some parts but it was the one with the most complicated and developed plot line. While the first two read like fairy tales this one seemed more like an actual fantasy novel- on less than 200 pages. <b>4 Stars</b>.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“Like a magpie, I am a scavenger of shiny things: fairy tales, dead languages, weird folk beliefs, fascinating religions, and more.”</i>
</b><br>-Laini Taylor in the Author's Note<br><br><br>In the end two things are certain:<br><br><u>One</u>: <b>I adore this author too much.</b><br>and<br><u>Two</u>: <b> This is a fantastic book.</b></span>

<div id="review_192470882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192470882" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192470882?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=made-me-think">made-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-liked-it">i-liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=strange">strange</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=original-and-creative">original-and-creative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-didn-t-see-that-coming">i-didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=short-and-sweet">short-and-sweet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=things-that-go-bump-in-the-night">things-that-go-bump-in-the-night</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192470882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15092646275615139974"><br/>Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br/><br/>I've been hearing lots of awesome things about <i>Lips Touch: Three Times</i>. And while it did not overly blow me away, it did not disappoint me either. There is something magical about the way Laini Taylor weaves her words into these three short stories. No doubt about that. <i>Lips Touch: Three Times</i> can best be described as a 3 course meal. <i>Goblin Fruit</i> can be likened to an appetizer: small and simple. It's not enough to calm your hunger, but enough to pique your interest for t</span>
  <span id="freeText15092646275615139974" style="display:none"><br />Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br /><br />I've been hearing lots of awesome things about <i>Lips Touch: Three Times</i>. And while it did not overly blow me away, it did not disappoint me either. There is something magical about the way Laini Taylor weaves her words into these three short stories. No doubt about that. <i>Lips Touch: Three Times</i> can best be described as a 3 course meal. <i>Goblin Fruit</i> can be likened to an appetizer: small and simple. It's not enough to calm your hunger, but enough to pique your interest for the remaining meal. She tells you just enough about the story to wet your palette, leaving you wanting more. So you continue onto your entre, <i>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</i>. You continue to devour the story laid out before you and before you know it, it has come to a subtle end. You are satisfied, but something better awaits you...dessert, <i>Hatchling</i>. You slowly savor every bite, tasting the individual flavors, teasing your taste buds. And it does not disappoint. <br /><br />Reading the above paragraph would make you wonder why I didn't give this book 5 stars, wouldn't it? I think short stories and I have issues. They just might not be my cup of tea. It's not that I found any of the stories bad, because they were very good. It just wasn't enough for me to truly connect to the characters. This book is most definitely a page turner and has the ability to keep you on edge. I was impressed with Taylor's ability to paint 3 vivid worlds/cultures with such few pages. That is a skill many YA authors seem to lack these days. Taylor is absolutely an author to keep an eye on. <br /><br />I didn't really know what to expect when I started reading this book. I was pleasantly surprised to see the beautiful drawings that prefaced each story. They told just enough of a part of the story to entice your curiosity. (Interestingly, they wre drawn by her husband. Thumbs up for the awesome team effort!) After finishing <i>Goblin Fruit</i>, the shortest of the three, I was surprised by the ending and intrigued. It was also my least favorite of the three simply because it caused images of Bella/Edward or Nora/Patch to dance on the edge of my memory. However, the story did not agitate me as theirs would. At least the ending matched where the story was heading.<br /><br /><i>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</i> was better for me and it neither surprised me nor upset me. It easily kept my interest, however, and the characters seemed slightly more relatable. Once again the writing was beautiful and I feel Taylor captured that time period perfectly. <br /><br /><i>Hatchling</i> was by far the darkest and coincidentally, my favorite. It's also the longest story of the three. I was really caught up in the mythology that Talyor used and was very interested in figuring out the mystery behind Esme's past. Let me just say that Laini Taylor is a master at the "show, don't tell" rule. The back story of Mab, Mihai, and The Queen was told so perfectly. She doesn't tell you everything all at once in a huge info-dump, but rather slowly reveals everything you need to know at just the right time. Honestly, I would have been happy to have an entire, full length story of <i>Hatchling</i>. It was just that interesting to me. <br /><br />All in all, I'm really happy I picked up <i>Lips Touch: Three Times</i> and I really can't wait to get my hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8490112.Daughter_of_Smoke_and_Bone" title="Daughter of Smoke and Bone by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of Smoke and Bone</a>.<br /><br />More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15092646275615139974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416435560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13063424108242906187"><b>The term this book brings to mind is "wickedly delicious."</b><br/><br/>It is the literary embodiment of my body's reaction to this gif:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449763063ra/17335043.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>UMPH. OKAY.<br/><br/>I originally put this off because I didn't feel like reading short stories that didn't have enough time to build a love for the characters or plot.<br/><br/>Oh how wrong I was. <b>This was absolutely extraordinary.</b> Laini Taylor is a mind-blowingly good writer with an insanely fantastic imagination. Each story (there are three as you may have guessed from the title) are vivid cr</span>
  <span id="freeText13063424108242906187" style="display:none"><b>The term this book brings to mind is "wickedly delicious."</b><br><br>It is the literary embodiment of my body's reaction to this gif:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449763063ra/17335043.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>UMPH. OKAY.<br><br>I originally put this off because I didn't feel like reading short stories that didn't have enough time to build a love for the characters or plot.<br><br>Oh how wrong I was. <b>This was absolutely extraordinary.</b> Laini Taylor is a mind-blowingly good writer with an insanely fantastic imagination. Each story (there are three as you may have guessed from the title) are vivid creative blendings of reality and fantasy, each with a single kiss that holds importance to the plot in some way. And no, it's not a cheesy romance type of kisses. They are dark and twisted and oh so powerful. The stories themselves aren't overtly sexual or explicit in any way, yet they have a very strong undercurrent of sensuality and physicality.<br><br>~*~*This also may make it onto my "all-time-favorites" bookshelf. We will see.*~*~ <br>(I usually let the book sit for a day before I make a decision.)<br><br>P.S. Also, in my hunt to find the perfect gif, I also found this was suitable as well.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453576190ra/17845354.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_200615828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200615828" />
    <a title="Taneika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika"><img alt="Taneika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564410672p2/5591031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200615828?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taneika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taneika" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika">Taneika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545055864" href="/book/show/6509152-lips-touch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200615828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15679648425637290979"><b>More of my reviews can be found at <a href='http://flippingthroughthepages00.blogspot.com/ ' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flipping Through the Pages</a>!</b><br/><br/>After picking up the little pieces of my brain and putting it back together after the masterpiece that was Daughter of Smoke and Bone. I thought I'd give my brain a little time to get working again before reading anything else by Laini Taylor. Lips Touch is wonderful. Just plain wonderful. It's a collection of three short stories that has kissing, magic, fantasy creatures and that beautiful, beautiful thing that is Laini Taylor's pros</span>
  <span id="freeText15679648425637290979" style="display:none"><b>More of my reviews can be found at <a href="http://flippingthroughthepages00.blogspot.com/ " rel="nofollow noopener">Flipping Through the Pages</a>!</b><br /><br />After picking up the little pieces of my brain and putting it back together after the masterpiece that was Daughter of Smoke and Bone. I thought I'd give my brain a little time to get working again before reading anything else by Laini Taylor. Lips Touch is wonderful. Just plain wonderful. It's a collection of three short stories that has kissing, magic, fantasy creatures and that beautiful, beautiful thing that is Laini Taylor's prose and imagination. I love adore and <i>envy</i> Taylor's imagination and her incredible story telling ability. Each short story just gets progressively better and better. You'll think you've had and incredible taste of what's in store after you've finished <i>Goblin Fruit</i> and just when you think it can't get any better then <i>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</i>, Laini Taylor pulls out the big guns and has <i>Hatchling</i> bewitching your mind (I've been re-reading Harry Potter...) and believe me, will have you begging for more!<br /><br /><b>Goblin Fruit:</b><br />In approximately 35 pages, Laini Taylor manages to write an incredible story with developed and complex characters and this to me, is a great feat. Kizzy is interesting, different and intriguing and has always been on the sidelines and has wanted that extra <i>something</i> in her life. This was the shortest of the three, but Kizzy’s story will have you laughing and doing double takes the entire time. It’s not as dark and gritty as the others, but the goblins and their fruit are fascinating, and is aplenty in so few pages.<br /><br /><b>Spicy Little Curses Such As These:</b><br />There was so much meaning in this story. Estella once made great sacrifice to a demon, and due to that, has been forced to make heavy decisions every day of her life whilst living in Hell. In order to save children, the demon says she must make sacrifices. She makes these sacrifices but when she is forced to place a curse on a baby named Anamique, the demon eventually gets more than he bargained for. Due to the curse, Anamique grows up mute, unable to even murmer a sound for the chance that it will kill anybody who hears it. She is teased and lives her life lonely until a soldier named James, finds her diary and falls in love with her. The romance that unfolds is breathtaking, beautiful and heartbreaking. Throughout, many sacrifices are made, but many lessons are learned.<br /><br /><b>Hatchling:</b><br />This was easily my favourite of the three! It BLEW MY MIND. The mythology was brilliant and once again, Laini Taylor has written a more complex and deep plot in 100 pages that many YA authors have tried (and failed) to do in their entire series. I WANT THIS MADE INTO A MOVIE. Or maybe I don't... Ohh, I don't know!! The world of the Druj is shocking and incredible. The Druj Queen keeps human children as pets until they reach child bearing age. This has so many stories rolled into one. Mab was the Queen's pet once, and her treatment was unbearable, it was absolutely horrible. When Mab is forced to have a child (literally, <i>forced</i>), we are told of how she managed to escape with her baby and what becomes of them once she becomes of child bearing age. Esme is incredibly three dimensional, and at first you may just think this is the story of Mab and Esme. But, it's not. This is only the tip of the iceberg and there is so much folklore and incredible world building. The 'villain' and characters who you think are just minor at first, turn out to have incredible stories of their own and Laini explores them so deeply and wonderfully that this will have you absolutely begging for more! <br /><br />The illustrations are mind blowing. To call them beautiful would do them injustice. At first they don't make sense, but once you've finished, you realise they capture the true essence of each story. Jim Bartolo is so incredibly talented!!<br />I would include photographs I took in this review, but I'm not very good at inserting images into GR reviews :) so they can be found on <a href="http://flippingthroughthepages00.blogspot.com.au/2012/03/lips-touch-three-times-by-laini-taylor.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog's review</a>!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15679648425637290979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261599639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10578433577818742020"><br/>Laini Taylor can string words together like pearls, her paragraphs glittering like diamonds on black velvet. She builds landscapes out of the ether and births characters of blood and solidity. When I read her I am a woman possessed -- consumed, enchanted and enthralled. I am a child, gripped by a child's wonder and insatiable hunger for stories. I am in love with this woman and her pink hair and beautiful, crazy mind (where I would live if it were only possible). <br/><br/>What kills me is that some of th</span>
  <span id="freeText10578433577818742020" style="display:none"><br>Laini Taylor can string words together like pearls, her paragraphs glittering like diamonds on black velvet. She builds landscapes out of the ether and births characters of blood and solidity. When I read her I am a woman possessed -- consumed, enchanted and enthralled. I am a child, gripped by a child's wonder and insatiable hunger for stories. I am in love with this woman and her pink hair and beautiful, crazy mind (where I would live if it were only possible). <br><br>What kills me is that some of the most heart-stuttering gorgeous prose I've ever read is to be found hiding behind some truly awful, misleading covers. It's amazing to me that Laini Taylor's fledgling, phenom writing career hasn't been completely sabotaged by the cover art chosen on her behalf. <br><br>Take this book for instance: the first cover is ... adequate, yet still terribly misleading of content and themes, while the second is just plain <i>bad</i>. Quite frankly, it stinks -- a Twilight-ish, vampish, Fifty Shades of Lipstick embarrassment. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1341175359l/6369113.jpg" width="185" height="255" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386905258i/7477143.jpg" width="185" height="255" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's just one example. Then came along <a href="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1338613368l/8490112.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">the cover</a> for <i>Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone</i>. Seriously? Try convincing someone that they MUST read this book working only with that confused and stupid cover. <br><br>Despite being constantly cover-challenged, Laini Taylor is blazing a permanent mark on the literary trail traveled by unique and intrepid storytellers. In the Author's Note, Ms. Taylor describes herself this way: <blockquote>Like a magpie, I am a scavenger of shiny things: fairy tales, dead languages, weird folk beliefs, fascinating religions, and more.</blockquote> I, for one, cannot wait to find out about the <i>and more</i>.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17572111313603066652">Lips Touch is a series of three short stories that centre around goblins, fairies and romance. My favourite of the three was the third tale, which is slightly longer than the rest. It follows Mab and daughter Esme, who are fleeing the pursuit of demons. What follows is a vividly retold tale about souls, rebirth and love. The world building for such a short piece was great and I actually craved more interaction between these wonderfully descriptive characters. I particularly liked the backstory f</span>
  <span id="freeText17572111313603066652" style="display:none">Lips Touch is a series of three short stories that centre around goblins, fairies and romance. My favourite of the three was the third tale, which is slightly longer than the rest. It follows Mab and daughter Esme, who are fleeing the pursuit of demons. What follows is a vividly retold tale about souls, rebirth and love. The world building for such a short piece was great and I actually craved more interaction between these wonderfully descriptive characters. I particularly liked the backstory for Mab, which gave depth to her character (and that of the queen).<br /><br />The other two stories I wasn't as enamoured with. They felt as though they were just skimming the surface of the emotional depth compared to the last tale, and both ended abruptly. <br /><br />Laini Taylor writes beautiful prose, but I think I'm just not really a fan of short stories. The last story is a solid 4 stars, but the other two are more of a 3.</span>

  <span id="freeText2046807793989137193" style="display:none">Goblin Fruit-3.5/5 stars. I enjoyed it because of course it was beautifully written and magical, but nothing here felt special.<br /><br />Spicy Little Curses Such As These- 5/5 stars. This story grabbed me from the beginning and had a fairy tale aura. Felt rather tragic.<br /><br />Hatchling- 5/5 stars. This one could be a book of its own. Such an imaginative, dark, intriguing story. <br /><br />For the record, I'm not a huge fan of short stories. But I'm thinking Laini Taylor can do no wrong.<br /><br />Also, gorgeous artwork.<br /><br />Basically, any artist/author dreams have been completely <s>inspired</s> shattered after reading this. Nothing I ever do could be this good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2046807793989137193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_126195157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126195157" />
    <a title="Mariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/647547-mariel"><img alt="Mariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451321467p2/647547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126195157?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariel" href="/user/show/647547-mariel">Mariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I don't want to live like this</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariel by: </span>
      Jareth in his tights said it would be fun
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126195157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16953388989328440911">I read the horoscope. It said that you would meet a tall and handsome stranger. Avoid all yellow fruits and scarves are for nooses to hang in an ever after. Lips should be colored artificially. Don't get red lips from kissing lots of the wrong boys and blue lips from the cold. It's l-o-v-e red. Maybelline makes it. She's born with it, of course. Don't look in the mirror. You might not be drop dead gorgeous and have to go on living. No invitations to the ballet in the mail this week... I'm a libr</span>
  <span id="freeText16953388989328440911" style="display:none">I read the horoscope. It said that you would meet a tall and handsome stranger. Avoid all yellow fruits and scarves are for nooses to hang in an ever after. Lips should be colored artificially. Don't get red lips from kissing lots of the wrong boys and blue lips from the cold. It's l-o-v-e red. Maybelline makes it. She's born with it, of course. Don't look in the mirror. You might not be drop dead gorgeous and have to go on living. No invitations to the ballet in the mail this week... I'm a libra and all other libras should do the same thing. We like dancing. There's a pretty little fabric pattern for all those born under the same moon and stars of moon and stars (stay under where you were born). Don't think for yourself. Fairy tale logic and curses and there are heroes and heroines and bad guys. It's all pretty simple. People are the same. Everyone dies and there are only two ways to go: Happy or dead. Ever after. <br /><br />Did you play Barbies and want to be a beautiful princess? Lips Touch: Three Times would resonate with the little girl that just knows she's going to grow up to be beautiful. The "geek" (Saved by the Bell version. Smoking hot in glasses that come off) that is going to go to a great college in six weeks and leave behind insecurity for evermore. Wasn't there a crack of loneliness, of doubt, for those who are not untouchable in their pristine beauty? She'll go to the ballet and can be a gorgeous singer without any practice at all. Not to mention the surpassing violin skills (that was too much!). My feet hurt. (And my eyes are still lodged in the back of my head after they rolled over Esme's instant prodigy skills as soon as she picked up the instrument.) It's not that easy. Dreams... My horoscope said it was possible. It says for tomorrow to beware of tall and dark strangers. Can I get a name instead of the dreamy vagueness? Maybe get to know them first? No? I don't see anything wrapped up... Maybe there's an ending in there after happily ever after of being pretty and perfect? <br /><br />Laini Taylor isn't a bad writer. She's just not enough of a story teller. I didn't move closer in front of the fire and hold my breath until everything worked out. Short stories aren't a lot of time for character development. But... I wanted character development. I wanted to know someone, anyone at all, in these stories more than the briefest contact at a six year old girl's Barbie doll play time wishes. Sultriness, wearing scarves in many different ways, artists drawing them because they were so uniquely beautiful (ahem unique? Really?), beauty and lots more beauty, perfect hair, perfect violin skills (come on! I HATE this about fantasy. They don't know when to stop piling on the perfectness). <br /><br />Did I lose the fairy tale dream? What was it, again? I thought it was the feeling to make you want to hold your breath and hope it worked out okay. Not that there were beautiful girls with perfect hair and the beautiful boys who loved them (they also have perfect hair). The second story was almost interesting. I liked it when the love interest James made his girl Anamique feel normal, that she might be able to cast off the big talk of curses and speak for herself. I liked it when he let her down by fearing its truth. But it was true! They fell in love at first sight. Pleeaaase. Not this again. I don't do first sight. You gotta write a real person for me to care about. I don't think that's too much to ask. I'm not six. What did it feel like to be silent for so long? Maybe what came out could have been than more than beauty. It could have been alive, rather than death. That would have been more interesting. Isn't that harder to not have the final ending? That would have been more difficult than a just because curse. Not knowing what was going to come next. You know, the pain of knowing what you want to say and not being able to say it? Saying the wrong thing? Because there isn't a fairy tale map that tells you what that right thing is. <br /><br />I liked the story of Mab (in 'Hatchling') and her life as a pet in the inhuman world of the Druj. Her neglect and cold days were more real to me than any of the cutesy shit about ballet every night, dancing like a fairy and diamonds in salt shakers. The violin playing skills! Come fucking on! Wasn't it enough that daughter Esme was inhabited by the druj queen all along? Wasn't there a point she was her own soul and had to WORK for something? Instant love with the boy in the flower shop... What about Mab? She had nightmares of being taken over by these druj who couldn't know what it was to steal the feelings of another. Isn't that something you'd feel something about? When did she get her own life? They were all pets because of the cuteness of their cutesy fairytale prettiness and greatness. I didn't like that. The Druj weren't human and didn't know what it was like to feel... Shouldn't that have been counteracted with something real? Something less... fairy tale? How about something hard and something won. That made it all a bit too hollow for me. I would have cared about feelings versus non feelings if there had been any. Since I don't fall at the feet of perfect beauty... Take my soul! Take mine! Nope. <br /><br />A kiss... Is a kiss just a kiss or does it lead to more? I don't care about the moment unless there's contact. There's no contact if there's no person! <br /><br />My horrorscope says there are no real characters. It's all a big fairy tale of the same old stories being told over and over again. No one steps off the path and says, "Hey, I'm going to think for myself. If you want to use your own voice don't worry that I can't handle it." Beauty is skin deep. Ideals matter more than the life the spark of an idea can have, and working to see it to fruition. People don't retell these old stories because there's something the same to connect to in others more than there is in what you want to be. I'm depressed. (It's just a book, Mariel. You've seen Disney films.) <br /><br />P.s. And what was that stuff about the kid souls from the earthquake in India getting saved in exchange for the voice of Anamique? Fairy tale stuff about the value of life and death like it was that easy? And then it was the old lady Estella's time to be up and what a relief it was? Why not try not messing with it in the first place and everyone lives and speak for themselves? (Am I living a fairy tale?) I'm still depressed in this p.s. <br /><br />P.s.s. And Kizzy didn't know anything on her own. It was all stuff her "weird" old world family told her. (Big deal if she knows songs in Basque. So what if Basque is too hard for me. I've got Basque relatives too, though. You don't hear me wailing about it.) She was the least real of the three girls. "I wanna be beautiful!" Cliche. Guess it was supposed to be relate able. There can be universal shit of a cute boy and teen romance. But maybe there could have been more to it than that? Kizzy could have known something on her own! Anything. Please. Real characters. Please! I don't care if they will get invited to dinner parties in adulthood! That's not growing up! Cries. I kinda hated this sometimes. Why did she feel so ashamed of her family and was so rude to her family and wanted to be kissed by beautiful people? Why couldn't she feel empty when she got what she wanted? Instead of being dead? Why couldn't she have wanted something for herself than a lusty dream? Why not? What was the point of retelling the story if it wasn't about why people want fairy tales? They want them like how sex looks good to the horny. Then the fairy tale should end and there should be something left alive in its wake. Lips Touch didn't have that. It's kinda empty. And I'm going to go read something else because I want something else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16953388989328440911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1235606180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1235606180" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1235606180?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=prosegasm">prosegasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1235606180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11445861429352283891">This book was a beautiful surprise. Everything was beautiful in it. Writing, characters, plot... everything. All three stories—<i>Goblin Fruit</i>, <i>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</i> and <i>Hatchling</i>—in this pretty book were wonderful. I'm in love with it.<br/><br/>The three stories involved a kiss—hence the title—that would mean something important (in a soul level) to the kisser.<br/><br/>The first one—<i>Goblin Fruit</i>—is the shortest of the three. It's about how Goblin men lure young girls. A long time ago, they did it by offe</span>
  <span id="freeText11445861429352283891" style="display:none">This book was a beautiful surprise. Everything was beautiful in it. Writing, characters, plot... everything. All three stories—<i>Goblin Fruit</i>, <i>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</i> and <i>Hatchling</i>—in this pretty book were wonderful. I'm in love with it.<br><br>The three stories involved a kiss—hence the title—that would mean something important (in a soul level) to the kisser.<br><br>The first one—<i>Goblin Fruit</i>—is the shortest of the three. It's about how Goblin men lure young girls. A long time ago, they did it by offering the girls tasteful fruits, but now, what are their new “fruits”? And is Kizzy (the heroine in this story) going to yield?<br><br><i>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</i> revolves around a girl with a curse—her voice kills anyone who listens to it. Matters get complicated when she falls in love and her lover wants her to speak. This one had a fairy-tale feel into it. Of all the stories, this one was the one I enjoyed the less... but calm down, I really liked it, believe it or not.<br><br>And the last one, and also the longest one,—<i>Hatchling</i>—starts when a girl's left eye changes from brown to pale blue just like that. Her mother is worried about her and she feels something is wrong. What is it and is she in danger? This one was my favorite.<br><br>Even the artwork in this book is beautiful! It's filled with many amazing illustrations that not only are they good companions to the stories but also great works of art. And do you know who did them? It was Laini's husband. What a team, isn't it?<br><br>The writing is beautiful, beautiful, beautiful, beautiful. I think I've overused that word in just one review, but who cares?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427846645ra/14327684.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now, before finishing, let me rant about something. But first, let's look at the blurb for this book: <b>In the style of Stephenie Meyer, three tales of supernatural love that all hinge on a life-changing kiss.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427846645ra/14327685.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Listen, I read <i>Twilight</i> last year, and in my opinion, there are no books more opposite than these two. No, just no. If you fear this is a <i>Twilight</i> fanfiction, then stop your worries. <b>They are not similar at all.</b> And please, don't ever compare a work of art with such an atrocity as <i>Twilight</i> is. Please and thank you. You think you're attracting readers? No. You <b>repel</b> them.<br><br>I may not have liked <i>Daughter of Smoke And Bone</i> a lot, but I fell in love with this book. You wish to read a book in which you can clearly see that the author put a lot of his/herself in it? <b>Then read this.</b> You will surely enjoy it. My only complaint is that it was too short and it all ended too fast.<br><br>Now, excuse me while I kiss this book and wait for the atrocious consequence that follows.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11445861429352283891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_92910430" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92910430" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89505-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534043413p2/89505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92910430?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/89505-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89505-jean?shelf=youngadult-fiction">youngadult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89505-jean?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92910430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1583916560403645090">I only read the first of the 3 supernatural tales in this book--"Goblin Fruit." (And I apologize to those who enjoyed it!) <br/><br/>The mood is heavy with superstition, slaughter and blood and flesh and titillation. In case grandma's trusty knife isn't enough, the element of danger is further highlighted by several appearances of the word rape, unsubtly used, for example, when peacocks in the farmyard don't screech or caw--they scream "rape." <br/><br/>The story is driven by the theme of lust despite (or heightene</span>
  <span id="freeText1583916560403645090" style="display:none">I only read the first of the 3 supernatural tales in this book--"Goblin Fruit." (And I apologize to those who enjoyed it!) <br /><br />The mood is heavy with superstition, slaughter and blood and flesh and titillation. In case grandma's trusty knife isn't enough, the element of danger is further highlighted by several appearances of the word rape, unsubtly used, for example, when peacocks in the farmyard don't screech or caw--they scream "rape." <br /><br />The story is driven by the theme of lust despite (or heightened by) a clear threat of danger to one's self. I have no objection to the supernatural setting--ghosts and upturned earth, or the theme of longing and desire. But the motifs are shallow and exploitative: horny teenage girls risking brutality and death for desire. Or, unnoticed or under-confident girls being easy sexual prey. Additionally, although the main character's actions and some of her inner thoughts are the subject of the narration as if she were our heroine--those readers who would prefer her objectification and victimization are also thoroughly indulged. Ick. <br /><br />If you dislike the Twilight series, you might dislike this too! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1583916560403645090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1688277178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1688277178" />
    <a title="Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52489703-taylor"><img alt="Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542815566p2/52489703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688277178?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor" href="/user/show/52489703-taylor">Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688277178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17458943107614912546"><b>4.5</b> <br/><br/><i>"The wicked in this part of the world endured rueful decades of early death, and the Fire burned hot and bright and remade them all, and they were all in their turn born back into the world as carp and macaques and salamanders and mosquitoes with no recollection of their human lives or the Fire that followed, but only faint memories of music, like wisps of a dream, from their last glimmering moments in Hell."</i><br/><br/>...<br/><br/>Well, <b>Laini Taylor is a goddess.</b> And this book and <i>Strange the Dreamer</i> are proof.</span>
  <span id="freeText17458943107614912546" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b> <br /><br /><i>"The wicked in this part of the world endured rueful decades of early death, and the Fire burned hot and bright and remade them all, and they were all in their turn born back into the world as carp and macaques and salamanders and mosquitoes with no recollection of their human lives or the Fire that followed, but only faint memories of music, like wisps of a dream, from their last glimmering moments in Hell."</i><br /><br />...<br /><br />Well, <b>Laini Taylor is a goddess.</b> And this book and <i>Strange the Dreamer</i> are proof.<br /><br /><i>Lips Touch Three Times</i> is a collection of three short stories with beautiful illustrations by Laini Taylor's husband, Jim Di Bartolo. This has been on my radar for quite some time, and <b>I'm so glad I've finally read this.</b><br /><br />This book is <b>
  <i>gorgeous</i>
</b>.<br /><br />Laini Taylor's writing is like drifting through a waking dream. It's vivid and rich, but it never feels too purple. There were moments in this collection where I'd come up for air and realize that my reality <i>wasn't</i> this book, and <b>I was genuinely sad.</b> It's hard to describe how breathtaking Laini's prose truly is.<br /><br />I'll give you a taste of her words:<br /><br /><br /><br /><i>“Kissing can ruin lives. Lips touch sometimes teeth clash. New hunger is born with a throb and caution falls away. A cursed girl with lips still moist from her first kiss might feel suddenly wild like a little monsoon. She might forget her curse just long enough to get careless and let it come true. She might kill everyone she loves.<br /><br />She might and she might not.”</i><br /><br />...<br /><br /><i>"Staring at her face, she began to fancy her outer layer had begun to melt away while she wasn't paying attention, and something - some new skeleton - was emerging from beneath the softness of her accustomed self. With a deep, visceral ache, she wished her true form might prove to be a sleek and shining one, like a stiletto blade slicing free of an ungainly sheath. Like a bird of prey losing its hatchling fluff to hunt in cold, magnificent skies. That she might become something glittering, something startling, something dangerous."</i><br /><br /><br /><br />Each story was fantastic in its own way. <i>Goblin Fruit</i> was dark and delicious, and it was so easy to connect with the main characters' dreams and desires. Kizzy lives in our world and goes to high school like every other teenager, but her life is anything but normal. <b>Ghosts haunt her yard, old stories bleed through her family's past, and monsters lurk in unexpected places.</b> It thrilled and terrified me, every second of it. <br /><br /><i>Spicy Little Curses Such as These</i> had setting and atmosphere <i>for days</i> I adored how Hell and the afterlife played a huge role in this story, and the characters were all delightful. The ending gave me <b>chills</b>, and I was enthralled with Laini's portrayal of young love and the difficulties that come with it. <br /><br />My one complaint with this entire collection was the fact that <i>Spicy Little Curses</i> took place in colonial India. <b>All of the central characters were white</b>, which didn't make sense to me.<br /><br />The last story, <i>Hatchling</i>, floored me. How the hell am I supposed to cope? <b>I'm obsessed and <i>I need a full-length novel.</i></b> The story was so intricate and complex, and the way everything connected in the end was <b>pure magic.</b> I can't breathe and I'm so in love.<br /><br />I adored how the illustrations for each story were placed at the beginning; as I read each tale, I was able to piece together the world and the narrative based on Di Bartolo's gorgeous artwork. <b>It gives a taste of each story to come, and I couldn't have been happier.</b><br /><br />It's strange. All three stories were so different, but each one left me...<b>aching.</b> There's a sense of longing I feel every time I read Laini's writing. It's like her words sing to my soul in such a way that it wants to lift out of my chest. <b>That's the best way I can describe how gorgeous her work really is.</b><br /><br />This was so so <i>so</i> good. If you're a fan of beautiful writing, or just want a wonderful short story collection to fly through, <b>pick this up.</b> It might not be for everyone, but it certainly sang to my dark, twisted, romantic little heart.<br /><br />...<br /><br /><i>“Is that all souls are for?" Esmé had asked him earlier. "For when we die?" <br /><br />Mihai could have laughed or cried when she'd asked him that. In all its simplicity her question was like cupped hands holding the meaning of his life. <br /><br />"No," he'd said. "They're for living too.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17458943107614912546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167944446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167944446" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167944446?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781441857781" href="/book/show/7638020-lips-touch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=graphic-illustrated-novels">graphic-illustrated-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167944446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4195482359221757032">Here’s a little synopsis of my thoughts as I listened to the first story:<br/><br/><i>…Remembering that fairy tales weren’t always about feisty princesses living happily ever after….<br/><br/>…Remembering that half of the time what they were about is “encouraging” teenage girls to keep it in their pants OR ELSE. Boo. On second thought, I want the princesses back.<br/><br/>…Hoping that this is heading in a different direction….<br/><br/>…Damn. If that’s all this is about then why am I reading it? Sure it’s gorgeous, but I could just be re</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4195482359221757032" style="display:none">Here’s a little synopsis of my thoughts as I listened to the first story:<br /><br /><i>…Remembering that fairy tales weren’t always about feisty princesses living happily ever after….<br /><br />…Remembering that half of the time what they were about is “encouraging” teenage girls to keep it in their pants OR ELSE. Boo. On second thought, I want the princesses back.<br /><br />…Hoping that this is heading in a different direction….<br /><br />…Damn. If that’s all this is about then why am I reading it? Sure it’s gorgeous, but I could just be reading Grimm’s Fairy Tales. This is just yet another case of recycling the old into the “next” big…<br /><br />Wait,<b> what?</b></i><br /><br />*Head explodes with awesomeness, and just a dash of guilt for not trusting my goodreads friends*<br /><br />Yep, I loved it. I hadn’t read any reviews before starting (not even the synopsis), so I really didn’t know what I was getting into, but I enjoyed it all the way through. This is a collection of three stories, which all feature different mythologies and worlds, but are tied together by the blissful, tantalizing, dangerous qualities of a first kiss. The third story is my favorite by far. I love the whole world that she builds in that one, and the dark and wanting demon race that inhabits it. I feel like the first story is an amuse bouche for the rest – which is handy, because it’s quite short. So, if you don’t like that one, it’s an easy out.<br /><br />This book made me realize that the current state of paranormal romance is such a shadow of what we once had. I feel like we all had this sort of hasty knee-jerk reaction. We wanted away with the obnoxious moralizing and scary demonic creatures, but we went too far, and lost so much of what made these tales great. We lost the shock and the fear, mostly. I am sure that there are other examples of fairy tale retellings done the right way, and I will be on the look-out for them. I would highly recommend this to anyone that can appreciate dark fairytales with unexpected endings.<br /><br />I listened to this one on audio, so I missed out on all the illustrations :(. Cassandra Campbell was excellent as always, though.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />The Smashing Pumpkins – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_-_Q8znGMRg" rel="nofollow noopener">Bodies</a> <br /><br />This was my favorite band back when I had my first kiss, so it seems appropriate. It’s also the first band I ever saw in concert, which was about one hundred times better than my first kiss.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4195482359221757032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The other two stories were very captivating and the writing is wonderful.<br/>I would definitely recommend Lips Touch. </span>

<div id="review_661400255" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661400255" />
    <a title="Theodora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21586560-theodora"><img alt="Theodora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521655166p2/21586560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661400255?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theodora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theodora" href="/user/show/21586560-theodora">Theodora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444731514" href="/book/show/24103818-lips-touch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661400255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17987629025417971064"><b>
  <u>Goblin Fruit</u>
</b><br/> <br/><b>3/5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>Kizzy wanted it all so bad her soul leaned half out of her body hungering after it, and that was what drove the goblins wild, her soul hanging out there like an untucked shirt.</i><br/><br/>Kizzy is 16 years old, smart but unenthusiastic, dreaming of other people's better, normal lives, and wishing for other girls' beauty. Kizzy's fierce with wanting and it makes her the perfect target for goblins. She has been warned of the danger of hungry souls yearning for forbidden things but th</span>
  <span id="freeText17987629025417971064" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Goblin Fruit</u>
</b><br /> <br /><b>3/5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Kizzy wanted it all so bad her soul leaned half out of her body hungering after it, and that was what drove the goblins wild, her soul hanging out there like an untucked shirt.</i><br /><br />Kizzy is 16 years old, smart but unenthusiastic, dreaming of other people's better, normal lives, and wishing for other girls' beauty. Kizzy's fierce with wanting and it makes her the perfect target for goblins. She has been warned of the danger of hungry souls yearning for forbidden things but that doesn't stop her from wanting.<br /><br />Dark, odd and hauntingly beautiful, Goblin Fruit is an enjoyable short story based on Christina Rossetti's Goblin Market.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Spicy Little Curses Such As These</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>4/5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>'That's the beauty of spicy little curses such as these, Estella.'</i><br /><br />Estella is a widow whose grief led her to Hell. Instead of going back to the world of the living with her beloved's soul, she returned tasked with a job - parley with the demon Vasudev for the souls of the children. From time to time, Vasudev allows Estella to save a few more children for the price of a curse. Such a curse is placed on Anamique, the grey-eyed daughter of the Political Agent in Jaipur, India. As Anamique grows old, she falls in love and puts her curse to the test. <br /><br />Spicy Little Curses Such As These is well-crafted and compelling, the prose lush and gorgeous. The characters are nicely developed and with depth (as much as possible in such a short story).<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Hatchling</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>5/5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Life in Herezayen was a brutality of numbness. Time dripped off the tips of icicles and Mihai's tribe did what they could to relieve the bleakness of their endless days.</i><br /><br />Six days before Esmé's fourteenth birthday, her left eye turns from brown to blue. Her sweet safe life shatters. She and her mother find themselves hunted by a mysterious race of shape-shifting demons. For better or worse, everything is about to change. <br /><br />Intricate and alluring, Hatchling takes the reader deep into a dark world of immortality and demons and love and souls. <br /><br /><b>*Trigger Warnings*</b> Sexual violence, slavery, child neglect.<br /><br /><br />Overall, <b>Lips Touch</b> is a beautifully written short story collection. Laini Taylor has a way with pretty words and enchanting worlds. I wish these short stories were full-length novels so they could last longer and have even more depth. <br /><br />P.S. The illustrations are wonderful and add some background to each story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17987629025417971064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_102786191" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102786191" />
    <a title="Laura Lulu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1648704-laura-lulu"><img alt="Laura Lulu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263959440p2/1648704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102786191?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Lulu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Lulu" href="/user/show/1648704-laura-lulu">Laura Lulu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1648704-laura-lulu?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1648704-laura-lulu?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1648704-laura-lulu?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1648704-laura-lulu?shelf=my-faves">my-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102786191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16273303910013631181">What a beautiful, <i>beautiful</i> book. It's a collection of 3 novellas, about girls mixing with goblins, demons, fae. The writing was just so lovely, Laini Taylor has such a (did I already say "beautiful"? Sorry. I need to get out my thesaurus--hold on...) such an <i>exquisite</i> way with words. It was just enchanting. <br/><br/>Here's the first page, just to give you a little idea:<br/><br/><i>There is a certain kind of girl goblins crave. You could walk across a high school campus and point them out: not her, not her,</i> her<i>. The</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16273303910013631181" style="display:none">What a beautiful, <i>beautiful</i> book. It's a collection of 3 novellas, about girls mixing with goblins, demons, fae. The writing was just so lovely, Laini Taylor has such a (did I already say "beautiful"? Sorry. I need to get out my thesaurus--hold on...) such an <i>exquisite</i> way with words. It was just enchanting. <br /><br />Here's the first page, just to give you a little idea:<br /><br /><i>There is a certain kind of girl goblins crave. You could walk across a high school campus and point them out: not her, not her,</i> her<i>. The pert, lovely ones with butterfly tattoos in secret places, sitting on their boyfriends' laps? No, not them. The girls watching the lovely ones sitting on their boyfriends' laps? Yes.<br /><br />Them.<br /><br />The goblins want girls who dream so hard about being pretty their yearning leaves a palpable trail, a scent goblins can follow like sharks on a soft bloom of blood. The girls with hungry eyes who pray each night to wake up as someone else. Urgent, unkissed, wishful girls.<br /><br />Like Kizzy.</i><br /><br />How captivating was that?<br /><br />And the artwork? Damn, where's that thesaurus again? Each story starts with a few pages of stunning artwork done in black and white with touches of red and pale blue. Gorgeous and breathtaking and frightening, all at once. It's rare to see a book where so much attention was paid to the <i>inside</i> being visually beautiful, and it made the book that much more wonderful.<br /><br />Go read this, now. This is what YA fantasy/paranormal should be. A book that treats it characters with beauty and respect, and doesn't make teenage girls into silly morons. <br /><br />A YA book that doesn't treat it's <i>readers</i> like silly morons.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16273303910013631181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j+npIUfpiHk84KS8hz/oRAR0hde9XFJtMA18q0B03HQihM5oSG0/vrcYdLTXQFtO30sLmLZcDa42HipxDutoQg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b+5oLo6kKZkQiXscEYvCl07kpYnqpRzVVcZkYwPoVovCg09ngSCeXptxqxRB9HGdldsrxuGlQxZT1TK5TXfivQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

And then one night, Abby\'s life is torn apart by two shocking revelations. First, she encounters a woman whose entire species was supposed to have been wiped out hundreds of years ago. Second, she learns that she isn\'t her father\'s only child after all. She has a twin brother, and now he too is being drawn into a clash between civilizations that threatens the entire world. A secret was hidden in Abby\'s mind long ago, and there are creatures that will stop at nothing to tear that secret out.  Ascension if the first book in the Demon\'s Grail series, in which an ancient war spills open into the modern day and one vampire is forced to finish the work her father started. Ends on a cliffhanger. <span id="freeTextContainer110240939732176551">Hi! I write fantasy books. My latest is STRANGE THE DREAMER, about a young librarian, a mythic lost city, and the half-human children of murdered gods. Check it out :-) Before that I wrote the DAUGHTER OF SMOKE & BONE trilogy, which has been translated into 32 languages. It's about a blue-haired art student raised by monsters, a broken angel, and a war that has raged for 1000 years in another worl</span>
  <span id="freeText110240939732176551" style="display:none">Hi! I write fantasy books. My latest is STRANGE THE DREAMER, about a young librarian, a mythic lost city, and the half-human children of murdered gods. Check it out :-) Before that I wrote the DAUGHTER OF SMOKE &amp; BONE trilogy, which has been translated into 32 languages. It's about a blue-haired art student raised by monsters, a broken angel, and a war that has raged for 1000 years in another world. I also wrote LIPS TOUCH: THREE TIMES, which was a National Book Award finalist, and the DREAMDARK books. As well as various short stories and novellas. <br /><br />Thanks for reading!! <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.lainitaylor.com">www.lainitaylor.com</a><br /><br />@lainitaylor</span>
  <a data-text-id="110240939732176551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6556598-lips-touch-three-times">Quotes from Lips Touch: Three...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Kizzy wanted to be a woman who would dive off the prow of a sailboat into the sea, who would fall back in a tangle of sheets, laughing, and who could dance a tango, lazily stroke a leopard with her bare foot, freeze an enemy's blood with her eyes, make promises she couldn't possibly keep, and then shift the world to keep them. She wanted to write memoirs and autograph them at a tiny bookshop in Rome, with a line of admirers snaking down a pink-lit alley. She wanted to make love on a balcony, ruin someone, trade in esoteric knowledge, watch strangers as coolly as a cat. She wanted to be inscrutable, have a drink named after her, a love song written for her, and a handsome adventurer's small airplane, champagne-christened Kizzy, which would vanish one day in a windstorm in Arabia so that she would have to mount a rescue operation involving camels, and wear an indigo veil against the stinging sand, just like the nomads.<br />Kizzy wanted.&rdquo;</span>
